2:27:1576:0:14:72:354:700:12:Times:12:Times:C:From Extreme to Mainstream: How Social Norms Unravel
2:28:1628:14:14:72:340:686:12:Times:12:Times:C:Leonardo Bursztyn, Georgy Egorov, and Stefano Fiorin
2:29:1680:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:C:NBER Working Paper No. 23415
2:30:1708:14:14:72:121:658:12:Times:12:Times:C:May 2017
2:31:1716:14:28:72:250:644:12:Times:12:Times:C:JEL No. C90,D03,D72,D83,P16,Z10
2:32:1747:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:C:ABSTRACT
2:33:1755:28:14:72:546:588:12:Times:12:Times:C:Social norms are typically thought to be persistent and long-lasting, sometimes surviving through 
2:34:1853:14:14:72:545:574:12:Times:12:Times:C:growth, recessions, and regime changes. In some cases, however, they can quickly change. This 
2:35:1946:14:14:71:546:560:12:Times:12:Times:C:paper examines the unraveling of social norms in communication when new information becomes 
2:36:2037:14:14:71:546:546:12:Times:12:Times:C:available,  e.g.,  aggregated through  elections.  We  build  a  model  of  strategic  communication 
2:37:2137:14:14:71:545:532:12:Times:12:Times:C:between  citizens  who  can  hold  one of  two  mutually  exclusive  opinions.  In  our  model,  agents 
2:38:2240:14:14:71:546:518:12:Times:12:Times:C:communicate their opinions to each other, and senders care about receivers' approval. As a result, 
2:39:2338:14:14:71:546:504:12:Times:12:Times:C:senders are more likely to express the more popular opinion, while receivers make less inference 
2:40:2434:14:14:72:546:490:12:Times:12:Times:C:about  senders  who  stated  the  popular  view.  We test  these  predictions  using  two  experiments.  In 
2:41:2541:14:14:72:545:476:12:Times:12:Times:C:the main experiment, we identify the causal effect of Donald Trump's rise in political popularity 
2:42:2638:14:14:72:545:462:12:Times:12:Times:C:on individuals' willingness to publicly express xenophobic views. Participants in the experiment 
2:43:2734:14:14:72:542:448:12:Times:12:Times:F:are  offered  a  bonus  reward  if  they  authorize  researchers  to  make a  donation  to  an  anti-
2:44:2834:14:14:72:545:434:12:Times:12:Times:C:immigration  organization  on  their  behalf.  Participants  who  expect  their  decision to  be  observed 
2:45:2940:14:14:72:546:420:12:Times:12:Times:C:by the surveyor are significantly less likely to accept the offer than those expecting an anonymous 
2:46:3039:14:14:72:546:406:12:Times:12:Times:C:choice.  Increases  in  participants'  perceptions  of  Trump's  popularity  (either  through experimental 
2:47:3145:14:14:72:545:392:12:Times:12:Times:C:variation or through the “natural experiment” of his victory) eliminate the wedge between private 
2:48:3242:14:14:72:545:378:12:Times:12:Times:C:and public behavior. A second experiment uses dictator games to show that participants judge a 
2:49:3336:14:14:72:545:364:12:Times:12:g_d0_f1:C:person less negatively for publicly expressing (but not for privately holding) a political view they 
2:50:3436:14:14:72:546:350:12:Times:12:Times:C:disagree  with  if  that  person's  social  environment  is  one  where  the  majority  of  people  holds  that 
2:51:3548:14:42:72:98:336:12:Times:12:Times:C:view.
2:52:3553:42:14:72:164:294:12:Times:12:Times:C:Leonardo Bursztyn
2:53:3570:14:14:72:200:280:12:Times:12:g_d0_f2:C:Department of Economics 
2:54:3593:14:14:72:179:266:12:Times:12:Times:C:University of Chicago
2:55:3614:14:14:72:165:252:12:Times:12:Times:C:1126 E. 59th Street
2:56:3633:14:14:72:162:238:12:Times:12:Times:C:Chicago, IL 60637
2:57:3650:14:14:72:124:224:12:Times:12:Times:C:and NBER
2:58:3658:14:28:72:188:210:12:Times:12:Times:C:bursztyn@uchicago.edu
2:59:3679:28:14:72:146:182:12:Times:12:Times:C:Georgy Egorov
2:60:3692:14:14:72:228:168:12:Times:12:g_d0_f2:C:Kellogg School of Management 
2:61:3720:14:14:72:191:154:12:Times:12:Times:C:Northwestern University
2:62:3743:14:14:72:169:140:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:2211 Campus Drive
2:63:3760:14:14:72:167:126:12:Times:12:Times:C:Evanston, IL 60208
2:64:3778:14:14:72:124:112:12:Times:12:Times:C:and NBER
2:65:3786:14:0:72:248:98:12:Times:12:Times:C:g-egorov@kellogg.northwestern.edu
2:66:3819:0:14:292:361:294:12:Times:12:Times:C:Stefano Fiorin
2:67:3833:14:14:292:454:280:12:Times:12:Times:C:Anderson School of Management
2:68:3862:14:14:292:474:266:12:Times:12:Times:C:University of California, Los Angeles
2:69:3899:14:14:292:422:252:12:Times:12:Times:C:110 Westwood Plaza C502
2:70:3922:14:14:292:411:238:12:Times:12:Times:C:Los Angeles, CA  90095
2:71:3944:14:0:292:405:224:12:Times:12:Times:C:stefanofiorin@ucla.edu
3:72:3966:0:28:72:185:690:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:C:1  Introduction
3:73:3981:28:16:72:540:662:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Social norms are an important element of any society:  some behaviors and opinions are socially
3:74:4076:16:16:72:540:646:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:desirable while others are stigmatized.  There is growing evidence that individuals care to a large
3:75:4175:16:17:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:extent  about  how  they  are  perceived  by  others  and  that  such  concerns  might  affect  important
3:76:4280:17:16:72:540:613:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:decisions in a variety of settings, from charitable donations (DellaVigna et al., 2012), to schooling
3:77:4381:16:17:72:540:597:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:choices (Bursztyn and Jensen, 2015), to political behavior (DellaVigna et al., 2017, Enikolopov et
3:78:4479:17:16:72:540:580:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:al., 2017, Perez-Truglia and Cruces, Forthcoming).  Moreover, these social image concerns matter
3:79:4575:16:17:72:540:564:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:both in interactions with other people from the same social group (Bursztyn and Jensen, 2015) and
3:80:4672:17:16:72:540:547:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in interactions with strangers, such as surveyors and solicitors (DellaVigna et al., 2012, DellaVigna
3:81:4773:16:16:72:540:531:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:et al.,  2017).  In particular,  even individuals with very strongly-held political views might avoid
3:82:4874:16:17:72:540:515:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:publicly expressing them if they believe their opinion is not popular in their social environment
3:83:4971:17:16:72:183:498:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(Bursztyn et al., 2016).
3:84:4995:16:17:88:539:482:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:A recent literature has documented the persistence of cultural traits and norms over long periods
3:85:5092:17:16:72:540:465:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of  time  (Voigtl ̈ander  and  Voth,  2012,  Fernandez,  2007,  Giuliano,  2007,  Algan  and  Cahuc,  2010,
3:86:5199:16:17:72:540:449:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Alesina,  Giuliano,  and  Nunn,  2013).   However,  little  is  known  about  what  factors  might  lead
3:87:5303:17:16:72:539:432:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:long-standing  social  norms  tochange,  or  even  more  so,  to  changequickly.   In  this  paper,  we
3:88:5406:16:17:72:540:416:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:argue that aggregators of private opinions in a society, such as elections, might lead to updates in
3:89:5506:17:16:72:540:399:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:individuals’ perceptions of what people around them think,  and thus induce fast changes in the
3:90:5601:16:16:72:540:383:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:social acceptability of holding certain opinions and in the likelihood that these opinions are publicly
3:91:5704:16:17:72:120:367:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:expressed.
3:92:5714:17:16:88:539:350:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Consider the support for the communist regime in the Soviet Union in the late 1980s.  Kuran
3:93:5805:16:17:72:540:334:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(1991) argues that many individuals opposed the regime but believed others supported it.  In that
3:94:5902:17:16:72:540:317:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:environment, a referendum on the regime would have quickly updated people’s opinions about the
3:95:5996:16:17:72:540:301:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:views  of  others.   Incorrect  beliefs  about  the  opinions  of  others  are  not  restricted  to  totalitarian
3:96:6109:17:16:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:regimes, where expressing personal views is often risky.  In fact, as we argue below, if most individ-
3:97:6211:16:16:72:539:268:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f6:B:uals assume that a specific opinion is stigmatized, the stigma might be sustained in equilibrium.1
3:98:6309:16:17:72:540:252:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:In this paper, we formalize this idea and test it using experiments with real stakes.  In our main
3:99:6407:17:16:72:540:235:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:experiment, we show that Donald Trump’s rise in popularity and eventual victory during the 2016
3:100:6502:16:17:72:540:219:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:U.S. presidential campaign causally increased individuals’ perception of the social acceptability of
3:101:6602:17:16:72:540:202:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:holding  strong  anti-immigration  (or  xenophobic)  views  and  their  willingness  to  publicly  express
3:102:6708:16:17:72:99:186:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:them.
3:103:6713:17:16:88:539:169:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:We present a simple model of strategic communication between individuals who can hold one
3:104:6802:16:14:84:539:153:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:1This  phenomenon  is  known  in  social  psychology  as  “pluralistic  ignorance”  (Katz  and  Allport,  1931),  where
3:105:6921:14:11:72:540:139:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:privately most people reject a view, but incorrectly believe that most other people accept it, and therefore end up
3:106:7036:11:11:72:540:128:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:acting  accordingly.   For  example,  in  1968  most  white  Americans  substantially  over-estimated  the  support  among
3:107:7158:11:11:72:540:117:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:other whites for racial segregation (O’Gorman, 1975).  A related concept is that of “preference falsification” (Kuran,
3:108:7276:11:11:72:540:106:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:1995):  people’s stated,  public preferences are influenced by social acceptability,  and might be different from their
3:109:7395:11:0:72:168:95:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:true, private preference.
4:110:7421:0:17:72:539:690:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of the two mutually exclusive convictions (e.g., xenophobic and tolerant).  Eachsenderdelivers a
4:111:7517:17:16:72:540:673:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:message (states his view) to arecipient, who in turn uses this message to make a Bayesian update
4:112:7613:16:17:72:540:657:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:on the sender’s true conviction (e.g., whether or not the sender is xenophobic).  In our setting, as
4:113:7713:17:16:72:540:640:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in DellaVigna et al.  (2017), lying is costly, so messages have some credibility; at the same time,
4:114:7812:16:16:72:540:624:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:citizens can pay this cost and lie, so communication need not be truthful.  Importantly, the sender
4:115:7911:16:17:72:540:608:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:has social image concerns:  he values other people’s perception of his type.  Thus, for example, if he
4:116:8013:17:16:72:540:591:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:thinks most other people are tolerant, he might want to hide his xenophobic views and pay the cost
4:117:8111:16:17:72:540:575:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of lying; conversely, if he believes that most other people are xenophobic, he would not only feel
4:118:8209:17:16:72:540:558:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:free to state such a view if he shares it, but may express xenophobia even if he is tolerant.  Thus,
4:119:8309:16:17:72:540:542:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:senders have incentives to ‘pander to the majority’. In the extreme cases we may have a ‘political
4:120:8407:17:16:72:540:525:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:correctness’ equilibrium, wherein all senders state the same view regardless of their true conviction,
4:121:8509:16:17:72:540:509:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:thus preventing learning about true convictions.  Receivers are Bayesian, and their perception of a
4:122:8608:17:16:72:540:492:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:sender of a message depends on the strategy that senders use.  In the example above, if xenophobic
4:123:8706:16:16:72:540:476:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:individuals say that they are tolerant because they believe that most are tolerant, then anyone who
4:124:8805:16:17:72:540:460:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:expresses  xenophobic  opinions  must  indeed  be  xenophobic.   At  the  same  time,  if  most  receivers
4:125:8911:17:16:72:540:443:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:are believed to be xenophobic so that even some tolerant people express such views, then a person
4:126:9008:16:17:72:540:427:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:stating xenophobic views is not necessarily a xenophobe, and thus will be judged less harshly by
4:127:9104:17:16:72:147:410:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:tolerant people.
4:128:9120:16:17:88:539:394:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Our model predicts, in particular, that a positive update in beliefs about the share of xenophobes
4:129:9218:17:16:72:540:377:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in a society makes xenophobic messages more likely.  Our framework thus illustrates how a shock to
4:130:9316:16:16:72:540:361:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the information possessed by individuals, such as an election where this particular issue (tolerance
4:131:9416:16:17:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:vs.  xenophobia) is salient, can rapidly change the social norm in communication behavior:  what
4:132:9512:17:16:72:540:328:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:was unacceptable and rarely, if ever, spoken, could become acceptable and normal in a matter of
4:133:9607:16:17:72:160:312:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:weeks, if not days.
4:134:9626:17:16:88:539:295:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Quite  interestingly,  the  logic  of  the  paper  suggests  that  information  aggregation  can  make
4:135:9728:16:17:72:540:279:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:an  ‘extreme’  topic  ‘mainstream’,  but  not  the  other  way  around:   such  a  shock  cannot  make  a
4:136:9833:17:16:72:540:262:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:mainstream topic extreme.  This is easy to see:  if a topic is mainstream and socially acceptable,
4:137:9931:16:17:72:540:246:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:individuals  know  how  widely  and  by  whom  each  opinion  is  shared,  in  which  case  information
4:138:10034:17:16:72:540:229:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:aggregation is unlikely to reveal new information.  Of course, if underlying fundamentals change –
4:139:10132:16:16:72:540:213:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:for example, more people become radicalized, or people become more judgmental of others – then
4:140:10226:16:17:72:540:197:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a certain viewpoint could move from mainstream to extreme.  However, since this involves changes
4:141:10322:17:16:72:375:180:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in fundamentals, this is likely to be a slow and gradual process.
4:142:10387:16:17:88:539:164:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:We test the model on both the senders’ and recipients’ sides using real-stakes experiments on
4:143:10480:17:16:72:540:147:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Amazon Mechanical Turk (MTurk) based on two recent votes.  On the sender’s side, we focus on the
4:144:10576:16:17:72:540:131:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:2016 U.S. presidential election.  Throughout his campaign, Donald Trump proposed, among other
4:145:10669:17:16:72:540:114:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:things, the construction of a wall separating the US and Mexico and a ban on Muslims from entering
4:146:10767:16:0:72:540:98:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the U.S. His popularity might thus send an informative signal to the population about the number
5:147:10864:0:17:72:540:690:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of people who sympathize with these proposals and thus about those who hold xenophobic views.
5:148:10957:17:16:72:540:673:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:As the experimental evidence we provide suggests, this signal is likely leading to a positive update
5:149:11057:16:17:72:540:657:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in  beliefs  about  the  share  of  xenophobes  in  the  country.   As  a  result,  Donald  Trump’s  electoral
5:150:11167:17:16:72:507:640:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:success potentially caused a shift in social norms regarding expressed views on immigrants.
5:151:11258:16:16:88:539:624:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:More specifically, in the two weeks before the election which took place on November 8, 2016,
5:152:11351:16:17:72:540:608:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:participants were offered a bonus cash reward if they authorized the researchers to make a donation
5:153:11450:17:16:72:540:591:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to  a  strongly  anti-immigration  organization  on  their  behalf.   Accepting  the  offer  is  therefore  a
5:154:11559:16:17:72:539:575:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:profitablexenophobic action.  At baseline,  participants who randomly expected their decision to
5:155:11655:17:16:72:540:558:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:be  potentially  observed  by  and  discussed  with  a  surveyor  in  a  future  interaction  (the  “public”
5:156:11763:16:17:72:540:542:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:condition)  were  significantly  more  likely  to  forgo  the  donation  bonus  payment  than  those  who
5:157:11868:17:16:72:540:525:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:expected their choice to be entirely anonymous (the “private” condition). This suggests the presence
5:158:11968:16:17:72:540:509:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of social stigma associated with the action. Before making the donation decision, a random subset of
5:159:12068:17:16:72:540:492:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:participants received information that positively updated their perceptions of Trump’s popularity
5:160:12165:16:16:72:540:476:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in  their  home  state  on  the  eve  of  the  election.   We  first  show  that  this  information  positively
5:161:12276:16:17:72:540:460:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:updates their beliefs about the local popularity of holding xenophobic views.  We then show that,
5:162:12373:17:16:72:540:443:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:for these participants, the wedge in the likelihood of undertaking the xenophobic action in private
5:163:12472:16:17:72:540:427:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and public disappeared.  This difference with respect to the baseline condition was driven entirely
5:164:12571:17:16:72:540:410:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:by an increase in the donation rate in the public condition, with no change in the private condition.
5:165:12672:16:17:88:539:394:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:We also exploited the “natural experiment” of Trump’s unexpected victory as an alternative
5:166:12762:17:16:72:540:377:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:“treatment” that could generate increases in the willingness to publicly express xenophobic views.
5:167:12860:16:16:72:540:361:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We  replicate  the  experimental  intervention  shortly  after  the  election,  restricting  the  design  to
5:168:12968:16:17:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the baseline condition with no initial information on Trump’s popularity.  We find that after the
5:169:13065:17:16:72:540:328:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:election, the wedge between private and public donation rates disappeared, even in the absence of
5:170:13162:16:17:72:540:312:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the experimental information intervention.  Again, this difference was entirely driven by an increase
5:171:13263:17:16:72:540:295:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in the public donation rate; the private donation rate remained unchanged from the pre-election
5:172:13358:16:17:72:540:279:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:survey.  Our results suggest that Donald Trump’s rise in popularity did not casually make these
5:173:13453:17:16:72:540:262:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:participants more xenophobic, but instead made the already more-intolerant ones more comfortable
5:174:13549:16:17:72:540:246:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:about publicly expressing their views. We also discuss suggestive evidence of the precise mechanisms
5:175:13649:17:16:72:169:229:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:driving our findings.
5:176:13670:16:16:88:539:213:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:A  second,  auxiliary  experiment  studies  the  receiver’s  side.   We  exploit  the  general  lack  of
5:177:13774:16:17:72:540:197:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:knowledge among MTurk users in Democrat-leaning U.S. states about the 2009 Swiss referendum
5:178:13865:17:16:72:540:180:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that banned the construction of minarets in that country.  We consider this an ideal setting for
5:179:13961:16:17:72:540:164:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:two reasons.  First, the topic of the referendum was closely aligned to that of our main experiment.
5:180:14061:17:16:72:540:147:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Second, the fact that most participants were unaware not only of the ban, but also of the fact that
5:181:14160:16:17:72:540:131:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the majority of the Swiss population supported it, allows us to manipulate their beliefs about the
5:182:14258:17:16:72:201:114:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:public support for the ban.
5:183:14285:16:0:88:539:98:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:After stating their personal views on whether the construction of minarets should be banned,
6:184:14378:0:17:72:540:690:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:participants  played  a  dictator  game  with  a  real,  anonymous  Swiss  person.   We  randomize  what
6:185:14482:17:16:72:540:673:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:information  was  given  about  the  Swiss  person  to  evaluate  via  revealed  preference  how  different
6:186:14589:16:17:72:540:657:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:information affected the participant’s opinion of that person. We focus on participants who reported
6:187:14689:17:16:72:539:640:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:beingagainstbanning the construction of minarets.  In the first treatment group, individuals who
6:188:14785:16:16:71:539:624:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:were randomly told that the Swiss person is in favor of the ban significantly reduced their donation
6:189:14885:16:17:71:539:608:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:levels in the dictator game, when compared to a control group where that piece of information was
6:190:14982:17:16:71:539:591:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:not provided.  In the second treatment group,  participants were additionally informed that 57%
6:191:15077:16:17:71:539:575:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of Swiss respondents also supported the ban, which positively updated participants’ priors about
6:192:15173:17:16:71:539:558:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the share of Swiss individuals in support of the ban.  Note that this was the actual support level
6:193:15271:16:17:71:539:542:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:for the ban in the 2009 referendum.  Thus, when informed that the Swiss person is surrounded by
6:194:15366:17:16:71:539:525:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f5:B:other people who support the ban, participants judged that person less negatively forexpressing
6:195:15461:16:17:72:540:509:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that view, understanding that he might have done so to pander to the majority:  donation amounts
6:196:15557:17:16:72:360:492:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:went up significantly compared to the first treatment group.
6:197:15617:16:16:88:539:476:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:A potential alternative interpretation is that participants judge the Swiss person less negatively
6:198:15715:16:17:72:540:460:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f5:B:forholdinghis opinion when the majority of Swiss support the ban,regardless of whether his support
6:199:15813:17:16:72:540:443:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:was expressed in public.For example, it could be that participants feel that they cannot blame a
6:200:15909:16:17:72:540:427:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:person for privately holding a view if that person is surrounded by many other people who also
6:201:16003:17:16:72:540:410:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:hold that view and who could also have influenced the private opinions of that person.  To directly
6:202:16102:16:17:72:540:394:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:rule out this alternative interpretation and confirm that our findings are driven by the anticipation
6:203:16203:17:16:72:540:377:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:by  participants  that  the  Swiss  person  might  have  had  strategic  reasons  to  publicly  express  an
6:204:16310:16:16:72:540:361:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:intolerant view, we also ran an additional experiment emphasizing that the Swiss person’s opinion
6:205:16407:16:17:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:was expressedanonymously.  In that treatment, informing participants of a higher level of public
6:206:16503:17:16:72:415:328:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:support for the ban in Switzerland doesnotincrease donation amounts.
6:207:16571:16:17:88:539:312:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Our results suggest that Trump’s rise in popularity and eventual electoral victory might have
6:208:16664:17:16:72:540:295:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:already  casually  changed  social  norms  regarding  the  expression  of  xenophobic  views  in  the  U.S.
6:209:16771:16:17:72:539:279:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Though we detect no changes inprivately-heldviews, we believe the findings on public expression
6:210:16866:17:16:72:540:262:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:are of great policy relevance.  For example, increases in public expression of anti-foreign sentiment
6:211:16967:16:17:72:540:246:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:might  also  lead  to  more  frequent  acts  of  hate  crime  against  foreign  minorities.   Indeed,  recent
6:212:17076:17:16:72:540:229:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:reports indicate a steep increase in the number of hate crimes against these groups throughout the
6:213:17174:16:16:72:540:213:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:campaign period, and especially after Donald Trump’s election.  For example, a recent report by the
6:214:17273:16:17:72:540:197:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Center for the Study of Hate and Extremism indicates that across eight major metropolitan areas
6:215:17368:17:16:72:540:180:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in the U.S., the number of hate crimes increased by more than 20% in 2016 (CSBS, 2017).  This
6:216:17461:16:17:72:540:164:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:increase is significantly larger in both absolute and relative terms than any year-to-year increase in
6:217:17563:17:16:72:540:147:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:hate crimes in these cities since 2010.  Increases in public expression of hate against some minorities
6:218:17666:16:17:72:540:131:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:might also spur increases in expression of hate against other minorities.  For example,  the same
6:219:17763:17:16:72:540:114:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:report shows that hate crimes against blacks and Jews in New York City also increased substantially
6:220:17862:16:0:72:540:98:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:between March 2016 and March 2017.  More common public expression of certain views might also
7:221:17956:0:17:72:540:690:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:facilitate coordination for large-scale actions, such as demonstrations and movements, and recent
7:222:18053:17:16:72:540:673:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:work has provided evidence that such demonstrations and movements might affect many important
7:223:18146:16:17:72:540:657:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:outcomes, from election results (Madestam et al., 2013) to the stock market valuation of different
7:224:18244:17:16:72:540:640:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:firms (Acemoglu et al., Forthcoming).  In addition, reductions in the stigma associated with holding
7:225:18344:16:16:72:540:624:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:previously-extreme views might lead to shifts in the language used in and reported by the popular
7:226:18441:16:17:72:540:608:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:media, and might also reduce the stigma associated with consuming and discussing certain news
7:227:18534:17:16:72:540:591:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:sources  on  the  far  side  of  the  political  spectrum.   For  example,  the  news  websiteBreitbarthas
7:228:18640:16:17:72:540:575:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:more  than  doubled  its  share  of  general  news  audience  between  the  end  of  2014  and  July  2016,
7:229:18747:17:16:72:540:558:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:reaching 9% of the market – 18 million visitors – that month.2Increases in public expression of
7:230:18842:16:17:72:540:542:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:such views can thus lead to increases in individuals’ overall exposure to them, and more exposure
7:231:18939:17:16:72:523:525:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:might eventually lead to changes in privately-held views, via persuasion or simple conformism.
7:232:19033:16:17:88:539:509:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Our results contribute to a growing literature that examines the impacts of political institutions
7:233:19131:17:16:72:540:492:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:on social norms and culture more generally.  This literature typically studies the long-run impact
7:234:19229:16:16:72:540:476:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of political institutions (e.g., Lowes et al., 2016); here we show that changes on the political side
7:235:19330:16:17:72:540:460:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:can lead to fast reversals in social norms.  Our paper also adds to a recent theoretical literature
7:236:19429:17:16:72:540:443:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:on  social  norms  (e.g.,  B ́enabou  and  Tirole,  2011,  and  Acemoglu  and  Jackson,  Forthcoming)  by
7:237:19534:16:17:72:540:427:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:studying  how  new  information  may  lead  to  the  unraveling  of  such  norms.   Our  findings  speak
7:238:19638:17:16:72:540:410:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to  a  cross-disciplinary  literature  on  the  consequences  of  political  action,  both  theoretical  (e.g.,
7:239:19749:16:17:72:540:394:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Lohmann,  1993)  and  empirical  (e.g.,  Madestam  et  al.,  2013).   Methodologically,  this  paper  also
7:240:19855:17:16:72:540:377:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:relates to a literature on the measurement of sensitive attitudes, which includes approaches such
7:241:19952:16:16:72:540:361:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:as the “randomized response technique” (Warner, 1965), the “list experiment” (Raghavarao et al.,
7:242:20048:16:17:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:1979), the “endorsement experiment” (Sniderman, 1993), and the “lost letter technique” (Milgram,
7:243:20144:17:16:72:540:328:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:1977).  In our study, the private donation decision provides a measure based on revealed preference,
7:244:20244:16:17:72:540:312:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and where concerns about social desirability are minimized due to anonymity.  Conceptually, our
7:245:20339:17:16:72:540:295:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:main experiment is novel since it exploits both experimental and natural occurring variation as two
7:246:20438:16:17:72:540:279:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:alternative approaches.  Randomized informational interventions are often subject to the criticism
7:247:20536:17:16:72:540:262:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of  not  being  entirely  natural,  while  before/after  designs  based  on  natural  variation  suffer  from
7:248:20645:16:17:72:540:246:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lack of true randomization.  In our setting, the two approaches yielded very similar results, which
7:249:20744:17:16:72:383:229:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:provides extra assurance of the validity of our tests of the model.
7:250:20811:16:16:88:539:213:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Theoretically, the two most important precursors to our paper are Bernheim (1994) and Morris
7:251:20903:16:17:72:540:197:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(2001).  Bernheim (1994) studies the behavior of individuals with social concerns and predicts the
7:252:21001:17:16:72:540:180:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:emergence  of  social  norms.   People  with  similar  preferences  will  adhere  strictly  to  such  norms,
7:253:21109:16:17:72:540:164:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:while  people  with  extreme  tastes  will  choose  not  to  do  so.   The  possibility  of  complete  pooling
7:254:21219:17:16:72:540:147:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and the resulting non-transmission of information is suggested in Morris (2001), where an advisor
7:255:21316:16:17:72:540:131:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:who  is  afraid  of  being  perceived  as  biased  ultimately  avoids  giving  advice  in  all  states  of  the
7:256:21427:17:15:72:540:114:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:world.  Our model can be viewed as combining and simplifying the two approaches to get a model
7:257:21521:15:0:84:397:99:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:A:2See https://fivethirtyeight.com/features/trump-made-breitbart-great-again/.
8:258:21598:0:17:72:540:690:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:with  straightforward  comparative  statics  results  that  highlight  the  role  of  individual  beliefs  and
8:259:21708:17:16:72:540:673:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:information shocks.  One can loosely view the model as adapting the binary message structure of
8:260:21803:16:17:72:410:657:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Morris (2001) to the social communication setting of Bernheim (1994).
8:261:21872:17:16:88:539:640:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Our  work  also  relates  to  existing  papers  studying  the  economic  consequences  of  conformity.
8:262:21974:16:16:72:540:624:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Prendergast (1993) identifies rational incentives for managers to conform to supervisors’ opinions in
8:263:22075:16:17:72:540:608:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:order to appear competent, which in turn hampers information transmission. Andreoni et al. (2016)
8:264:22172:17:16:72:540:591:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:study ‘conformity traps,’ situations where groups of individuals fail to coordinate on a beneficial
8:265:22271:16:17:72:540:575:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:action due to individual incentives to conform to the predominant and inefficient behavior.  In a
8:266:22368:17:16:72:540:558:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:laboratory experiment they find, in particular, that opinion polls can facilitate changes of norms
8:267:22466:16:17:72:540:542:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that benefit the group.  Their setting, however, is one of full information, and thus opinion polls
8:268:22565:17:16:72:540:525:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:facilitate switching from one equilibrium to another.  Our model has incomplete information and
8:269:22660:16:17:72:540:509:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:features a unique equilibrium, and elections can change the beliefs about the distribution of other
8:270:22759:17:16:72:540:492:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:people’s opinions (though we do not take a position on whether overcoming conformity is necessarily
8:271:22858:16:16:72:540:476:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:socially beneficial).  In a different setting, Kets and Sandroni (2015) study the trade-off between
8:272:22957:16:17:72:394:460:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the performance of conforming versus diverse groups of individuals.
8:273:23024:17:16:88:539:443:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The remainder of this paper proceeds as follows.  We introduce a simple framework formalizing
8:274:23117:16:17:72:540:427:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:our argument in Section 2. In Section 3, we present the design and results from the main experiment
8:275:23216:17:16:72:540:410:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:studying the 2016 U.S. presidential elections.  In Section 4, we present the design and results from
8:276:23316:16:38:72:363:394:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the auxiliary dictator game experiment.  Section 5 concludes.
8:277:23377:38:28:72:260:356:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:C:2  Theoretical Framework
8:278:23401:28:24:72:262:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:2.1  A model of communication

12:485:33413:33:23:72:160:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:2.3  Dynamics
12:486:33426:23:17:72:540:321:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Let  us  now  consider  a  simple  extension  of  the  previous  model  that  will  enable  us  to  study  how
12:487:33536:17:16:72:540:304:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:certain  shocks  to  the  underlying  parameters  affect  communication  strategies  within  the  society,
12:488:33642:16:16:72:540:288:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:as well as social learning.  There may be multiple reasons for shocks:  arrival of new information
12:489:33740:16:17:72:540:272:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that makes some people change their opinions,  a speech by an influential politician or celebrity,
12:490:33838:17:16:72:540:255:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:or others.  Here, we consider elections as a particular case of a shock that aggregates convictions
12:491:33937:16:17:72:540:239:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and allows citizens to learn about members of their society that they do not directly communicate
12:492:34034:17:16:72:100:222:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f6:B:with.6
12:493:34040:16:17:88:539:206:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Specifically, we consider a three-period model. In each of the periods, each citizen communicates
12:494:34137:17:16:72:540:189:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:with a continuum of other citizens, and we assume that in these communications he is both the
12:495:34230:16:16:72:540:173:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:sender and the receiver.  Informally, we think about citizens adopting a certain ‘persona’ for the
12:496:34328:16:17:72:540:157:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:whole period, and if what they learned during that period about the rest of the society suggests
12:497:34424:17:16:72:540:140:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:it would be better to act differently, they can send different messages in the subsequent periods.
12:498:34522:16:15:84:539:124:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:6Political campaigns that precede elections may, of course, persuade people to change convictions about issues or
12:499:34635:15:11:72:540:109:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:make some issues more salient than others.  This may also change communication strategies in the society.  Here, we
12:500:34750:11:0:72:385:98:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:only focus on the moment of elections as the source of the information shock.
13:501:34829:0:17:72:540:690:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Formally, we assume that each citizen is matched with three disjoint continua of other citizens, and
13:502:34929:17:16:72:540:673:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in each of the periods, he sends a message to all other citizens matched to him in that period and
13:503:35027:16:17:72:539:657:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:receives messages from all of them.7Before period 1, the share of citizens having convictionA, i.e.,
13:504:35127:17:16:72:540:640:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f4:B:p, is realized, and Nature instead sends a public noisy signal to all citizens, so citizens start period
13:505:35231:16:16:72:539:624:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:1 with a common belief that the share of citizens with convictionAisq.  They communicate in
13:506:35322:16:17:72:539:608:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f9:B:period 1, update onpand communicate in period 2.  Between periods 2 and 3, Nature revealsp
13:507:35412:17:16:71:539:591:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(e.g., through elections), after which the citizens have a final round of communication.  Such timing
13:508:35513:16:17:71:539:575:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:allows  us  to  compare  the  social  norms  learned  through  strategic  communication  (period  2)  and
13:509:35618:17:16:71:539:558:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the social norms learned through public information aggregation (period 3).  We do not introduce
13:510:35714:16:17:71:539:542:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:any discounting, but since each agent is infinitesimal and does not expect to change others’ beliefs
13:511:35814:17:16:71:539:525:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:for the subsequent periods, each agent would communicate to maximize his static payoffs with or
13:512:35909:16:17:71:169:509:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:without discounting.
13:513:35929:17:25:88:227:492:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:We have the following result.
13:514:35958:25:16:71:303:467:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f5:C:Proposition 4.Let againv=2√a2+8a+a.  Then:

13:531:36336:16:26:71:170:385:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:C:differently otherwise.
13:532:36358:26:16:88:539:359:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:This result is mainly of interest if the original belief was wrong.  Ifqis relatively close to12, then
13:533:36460:16:16:71:539:343:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f9:B:both messages are sent with positive probabilities.  Each citizen is then perfectly able to deducep
13:534:36559:16:17:71:540:327:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:from what they observe in period 1.  Indeed, suppose, for the sake of the argument, thatq≥12.  In

13:536:36745:16:17:71:540:294:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:values  ofq,z <1,  and  thereforepcan  be  perfectly  learned.   Once  this  is  the  case,  there  is  no

13:539:37002:17:16:88:539:244:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The pattern is very different ifqis not close to12(anda >1).  In this case, all citizens, regardless

13:542:37292:17:16:71:540:195:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:citizen makes any inference aboutp.  The second period is then identical to the first one.  However,
13:543:37392:16:17:71:539:179:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the true value ofpis revealed before period 3, and this can potentially lead to a different behavior.
13:544:37493:17:16:71:539:162:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Namely, ifq >12+v, so all citizens were sendingAin periods 1 and 2, then this will only continue
13:545:37589:16:18:72:540:146:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ifp >12+vas well, while ifp≤12+v, then some (or, in the extreme casep≤12−v, all) citizens
13:546:37678:18:15:84:540:128:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:7For example, suppose that citizens are randomly allocated in a unit cube with coordinates (x, y, z).  In period 1,
13:547:37793:15:10:72:539:113:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:citizen (x, y, z) communicates with citizens of the form (∗, y, z), in period 2, he does so with (x,∗, z), and in period
13:548:37913:10:11:72:539:103:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:3, he communicates with those of the form (x, y,∗).  Within a period, all citizens communicate simultaneously, so the
13:549:38030:11:0:72:390:92:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:message that a citizen sends is not affected by what he receives in that period.
14:550:38112:0:17:72:211:690:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:will start sending messageB.
14:551:38140:17:16:88:539:673:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:We thus observe the following.  If the original citizens’ beliefs about their fellow citizens are
14:552:38237:16:17:71:539:657:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:sufficiently moderate, the society is able to learn the true parameter through communication, and
14:553:38334:17:16:71:539:640:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:elections do not reveal new information and therefore do not lead to a change in behavior.  However,
14:554:38434:16:16:71:539:624:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:if the original beliefs led the society to a ‘political correctness’ equilibrium, then there is no learning
14:555:38541:16:17:71:539:608:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in communication.  In this case, elections can reveal new and surprising information, and thus can
14:556:38639:17:32:71:336:591:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lead to a discontinuous change in beliefs and behaviors.
14:557:38695:32:24:71:168:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:2.4  Predictions

14:560:38866:16:26:99:423:491:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:also increases the likelihood that the corresponding message is sent.
14:561:38935:26:16:79:540:465:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:(ii)  The  receiver’s  posterior  that  the  sender  who  sent  a  message  indeed  has  the  corresponding
