14:566:39133:9:17:532:539:449:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f11:C:∪
14:567:39134:17:0:99:225:432:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f4:A:{1}, and it is U-shaped on
14:568:39160:0:12:229:239:441:11:g_d0_f16:8:g_d0_f6:?:(1
14:569:39162:12:0:235:250:429:8:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f4:?:2,1
14:570:39165:0:9:251:256:441:11:g_d0_f16:11:g_d0_f16:?:)
14:571:39166:9:25:256:385:432:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:?:, while always exceeding12.
14:572:39193:25:17:76:540:407:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(iii)  A shock that aggregates preferences in the society does not change individual behavior if the
14:573:39293:17:16:99:540:390:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:society was not in a ‘political correctness’ equilibrium.  If it was, then a shock may change
14:574:39386:16:38:99:143:374:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:behavior.
14:575:39395:38:27:71:426:336:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:C:3  Main Experiments: U.S. Presidential Elections
14:576:39443:27:17:71:539:309:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We developed two experiments with workers from the online platform MTurk.  A number of recent
14:577:39536:17:16:71:539:292:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:papers in economics have used the same platform to conduct surveys or experiments (e.g., Kuziemko
14:578:39633:16:17:71:539:276:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:et al.  2015, Elias et al.  2016).  The platform draws workers from very diverse backgrounds, though
14:579:39733:17:32:71:345:259:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:it is not representative of the U.S. population as a whole.
14:580:39792:32:23:71:225:227:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:3.1  Experimental Design
14:581:39816:23:24:71:287:204:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:C:3.1.1    Intervention Before the Election
14:582:39857:24:16:71:539:180:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:During the two weeks prior to the presidential election, we recruited participants (N = 458) from
14:583:39954:16:17:71:539:164:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the  eight  states  in  which  the  expected  probability  of  Donald  Trump’s  victory  at  the  state  level
14:584:40064:17:16:71:539:147:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:was 100%, according to the websitePredictwise:  Alabama, Arkansas, Idaho, Nebraska, Oklahoma,
14:585:40157:16:17:72:540:131:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Mississippi, West Virginia, and Wyoming.  MTurk workers with at least 80% approval rate could see
14:586:40254:17:16:72:540:114:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:our request, which was described as a “5 minute survey” with a reward of $0.50.  Each worker could
14:587:40352:16:0:72:540:98:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:participate in the survey only once.  Workers who clicked on the request were displayed detailed
15:588:40450:0:17:72:540:690:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:instructions about the task, and given access to links to the study information sheet and the actual
15:589:40550:17:16:72:397:673:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f5:B:survey.  The survey was conducted on the online platformQualtrics.
15:590:40616:16:17:88:539:657:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:After  answering  a  number  of  demographic  questions,  half  of  the  participants  were  randomly
15:591:40717:17:16:71:539:640:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:informed about the 100% local odds from the website (informationcondition) while the other half
15:592:40812:16:16:72:539:624:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:were not informed (controlcondition).8Though restricting to these states might affect the external
15:593:40910:16:17:72:540:608:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:validity of the findings, it also allows us not to worry about the role of heterogeneous priors (and
15:594:41010:17:16:72:540:591:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:updates) in response to an informational treatment:  the 100% forecast ensured that for this half
15:595:41107:16:17:72:540:575:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of the sample, the direction of the update in Trump’s perceived local popularity is either zero or
15:596:41205:17:16:72:210:558:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f6:B:positive, but never negative.9
15:597:41235:16:17:88:539:542:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Participants were then all asked to predict to share of individuals in their state that agree with
15:598:41333:17:27:72:304:525:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f6:B:a relatively strong anti-immigration statement:10
15:599:41382:27:17:99:512:498:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Both legal and illegal immigration should be drastically reduced because immigrants
15:600:41465:17:28:99:414:481:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:undermine American culture and do not respect American values.
15:601:41527:28:16:88:503:453:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:This provides a measure of the perceived local popularity of anti-immigrant sentiment.
15:602:41613:16:17:88:539:437:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:In the next part of the intervention, we measured the perceived social acceptability of strong
15:603:41707:17:16:72:540:420:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:anti-immigrant  sentiment  using  a  donation  experiment  with  real  stakes.   Participants  were  first
15:604:41813:16:16:72:540:404:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:told that they would be given the possibility to make a donation to a randomly drawn organization
15:605:41910:16:17:72:540:388:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that  could  either  be  anti-  or  pro-immigration,  to  ensure  that  participants  would  not  associate
15:606:42017:17:16:72:540:371:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the experimenters with a specific political view.  To maximize power and avoid direct deception,
15:607:42113:16:17:72:540:355:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the randomization was such that more than 90% of participants (N=428) would get assigned the
15:608:42205:17:16:72:539:338:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:organization  we  were  interested  in:  theFederation  of  American  Immigration  Reform.   To  make
15:609:42306:16:17:72:540:322:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:sure participants were aware of the organization’s very strong anti-immigration stance, a few more
15:610:42404:17:15:72:453:305:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:details about the organization and its founder were provided in the experiment:
15:611:42483:15:11:84:305:290:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:A:8See the survey scripts in the Supplemental Appendix.
15:612:42536:11:15:84:539:279:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:9Eliciting priors in the control group to assess the direction of the update would have been challenging since the
15:613:42650:15:11:72:540:264:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:forecast  information  was  available  online.   Therefore,  asking  the  question  before  the  donation  decision  could  have
15:614:42778:11:11:72:540:253:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:undone the treatment.  Answers to the question if asked after the donation decision could have been affected by the
15:615:42893:11:7:72:408:242:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:decision itself and by the private/public condition later assigned to the participant.
15:616:42979:7:15:80:539:235:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:10Here  we  describe  the  protocol  of  the  experiment  as  it  was  registered  on  the  AEA  RCT  registry  with  number
15:617:43103:15:11:72:540:220:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:AEARCTR-0001752.  As described in the registry,  we planned to reach 400 individuals by November 7 – the day
15:618:43211:11:11:72:540:209:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:before the election and thus conceptually the last day in which the survey could be done (also pre-registered as the
15:619:43327:11:11:72:540:198:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:trial end date).  In the piloting phase (on October 26 and 27,)  we were able to recruit 184 participants.  We thus
15:620:43442:11:11:72:540:187:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:expected not to have any issue recruiting 400 more subjects in the eight days between October 31 and November 7,
15:621:43554:11:11:72:540:176:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:given that in two days we were able to survey nearly half of that sample size.  However, only 274 MTurk workers
15:622:43665:11:11:72:540:165:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:selected themselves into the study during the registered trial dates.  The number of active MTurk workers in these
15:623:43779:11:11:72:540:154:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:states  is  lower  than  we  had  originally  expected  (and  to  our  knowledge  no  estimates  of  the  MTurk  population  in
15:624:43906:11:11:72:540:143:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:those states exist), which made it difficult to recruit enough participants before the election.  In order to reach the
15:625:44025:11:10:72:540:132:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:desired  (and  registered)  sample  size,  we  decided  to  include  individuals  who  participated  in  the  pilot  experiment
15:626:44152:10:11:72:540:122:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:conducted before the registration with nearly identical versions of the protocol.  In particular, both the wording of
15:627:44269:11:11:72:540:111:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:the informational treatment and the wording of the donation decision were completely unchanged.  If we restrict the
15:628:44384:11:11:72:540:100:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:analysis to the 274 subjects who followed the registered protocol,  results are directionally similar,  as discussed in
15:629:44503:11:0:72:132:89:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:Subsection 3.3.
16:630:44520:0:17:99:519:690:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f12:A:The Federation for American Immigration Reform (FAIR) is animmigration-reduction
16:631:44600:17:16:99:512:673:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f4:A:organizationof concerned individuals who believe that immigration laws must be re-
16:632:44682:16:17:99:512:657:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:formed, and seeks to reduce overall immigration (both legal and illegal) into the United
16:633:44770:17:16:99:512:640:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:States.  The founder of FAIR is John Tanton, author of ‘The Immigration Invasion’ who
16:634:44855:16:16:99:512:624:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:wrote “I’ve come to the point of view that for European-American society and culture
16:635:44939:16:29:99:461:608:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:to persist requires a European-American majority, and a clear one at that.”
16:636:45014:29:16:88:539:579:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Participants were then asked if they would like to authorize the researchers donate $1 to that
16:637:45108:16:17:71:539:563:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:organization  on  their  behalf.   The  money  would  not  come  from  the  subject’s  $0.50  payment  for
16:638:45214:17:16:71:539:546:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:participation in the study.  Moreover, the participant would also be paid anextra$1 (or about 1/6
16:639:45311:16:16:71:539:530:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of an hourly wage on MTurk) if he/she authorized the donation.  Rejecting the donation would not
16:640:45407:16:17:71:539:514:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:affect the monetary payoffs to the participants in any way other than through the loss of this extra
16:641:45507:17:16:71:110:497:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:amount.
16:642:45514:16:17:88:539:481:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:In  addition  to  the  original  randomization  of  informing  subjects  about  Trump’s  probability
16:643:45614:17:16:71:539:464:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of victory in the participant’s state,  we introduced a second layer of cross-randomization at the
16:644:45712:16:17:71:539:448:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:donation stage.  Half of the participants were assured that their donation authorization would be
16:645:45809:17:16:71:539:431:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:kept completely anonymous, and that no one, not even the researchers would be able to match their
16:646:45906:16:16:71:539:415:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:decision to their name: we refer to this condition as thePrivatecondition.  Specifically, participants
16:647:46008:16:29:71:118:399:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:were told:
16:648:46018:29:16:99:513:370:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f12:A:Note:  just like any other answer to this survey, alsoyour donation decision will be
16:649:46102:16:16:99:512:354:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f4:A:completely anonymous.  No one, not even the researchers, will be able to match your
16:650:46185:16:29:99:207:338:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:decision to your name.
16:651:46207:29:16:88:539:309:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The other half of the subjects were instead informed, right before the donation question was
16:652:46299:16:17:71:539:293:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:displayed to them, that they might be personally contacted by the research team to verify their
16:653:46394:17:16:71:539:276:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f5:B:answers to the questions in the remaining part of the survey:  this is what we refer to as thePublic
16:654:46494:16:28:72:119:260:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:condition.
16:655:46504:28:17:99:512:232:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Important: in order to ensure the quality of the data collected, a member of the research
16:656:46593:17:16:99:512:215:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:teammight personally contact youto verify your answers to the next question and
16:657:46672:16:28:99:188:199:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:the following ones.
16:658:46691:28:17:88:539:171:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Names and contact information were not collected during the intervention, since the practice
16:659:46783:17:16:72:540:154:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:is not allowed on MTurk.  As a result, it was not possible to credibly lead participants to believe
16:660:46882:16:16:72:540:138:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that their decision would be observed by other individuals, for example, from their state.  However,
16:661:46982:16:17:72:540:122:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:on MTurk it is possible to contact participants individually on the platform via their worker ID.
16:662:47079:17:16:72:540:105:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We were therefore able to minimize the use of deception since the decision was anonymous yet re-
16:663:47175:16:0:72:540:89:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:searchers could still potentially contact participants (moreover, participants in the public condition
17:664:47279:0:17:72:540:690:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:might have believed that they would be asked for personal information in case they were contacted
17:665:47376:17:16:72:540:673:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:later on).  As mentioned before, social acceptability with respect to surveyors and solicitors is also
17:666:47478:16:17:72:540:657:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:informative to the study of social pressure and social image concerns, as examined in DellaVigna
17:667:47574:17:31:72:275:640:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:et al.  (2014) and DellaVigna et al.  (2017).
17:668:47619:31:24:72:282:609:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:C:3.1.2    Intervention After the Election
17:669:47659:24:16:72:540:585:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We also exploited the natural experiment of Trump’s unexpected victory as an alternative “treat-
17:670:47755:16:17:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ment” potentially leading to an increase in the social acceptability of holding xenophobic views.  We
17:671:47856:17:16:72:540:552:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:repeated the experimental intervention in the same states during the first week after the election,
17:672:47955:16:17:72:540:536:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:restricting the design to the control condition with no additional initial information on Trump’s
17:673:48052:17:16:72:540:519:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:popularity.  We recruited both subjects who had participated before the election (N = 168; 166 of
17:674:48149:16:16:72:540:503:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:them assigned to the anti-immigration organization) and new participants (N = 218; 215 assigned
17:675:48244:16:17:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to that organization).  Based on naturally occurring variation, we can assess the impact of Trump’s
17:676:48343:17:32:72:399:470:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:electoral victory on the perceived social acceptability of xenophobia.
17:677:48413:32:24:72:424:438:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:3.2  Linking the Experiment to the Theoretical Framework
17:678:48469:24:16:72:539:414:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:In what follows, we assume thatAis the xenophobic conviction, whileBis the opposite (tolerant)
17:679:48563:16:16:72:540:398:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:one.   In  the  main  experiment,  the  communication  is  between  the  subject  (thesender)  and  the
17:680:48666:16:17:72:539:382:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:researcher (thereceiver).  Moreover,qhere corresponds to the sender’s beliefs about the share of
17:681:48762:17:16:72:539:365:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:xenophobes in the country.  We consider two treatments that test the effect of manipulatingqon the
17:682:48860:16:17:72:540:349:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:likelihood that a xenophobic message is sent, thus testing the comparative static result associated
17:683:48959:17:28:72:198:332:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:withqfrom Proposition 2:
17:684:48983:28:17:88:540:304:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f4:A:•Treatment 1: the researchers communicate to the subject that Trump is winning for sure in
17:685:49073:17:25:99:151:287:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:their state.
17:686:49085:25:28:88:285:262:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f4:A:•Treatment 2:  Trump wins the election.
17:687:49124:28:17:88:539:234:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Note that though both treatments increaseq, their effect might operate through different chan-
17:688:49218:17:16:72:540:217:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:nels.  In particular, since Treatment 1 provides information about the area where the sender lives,
17:689:49317:16:17:72:540:201:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the effect is likely operating through the sender updating his beliefs about what the receiver thinks
17:690:49418:17:16:72:540:184:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of him in the absence or in the presence of a xenophobic message being communicated.  On the
17:691:49510:16:16:72:540:168:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:other hand, since Treatment 2 provides information at the country level, it might also lead to an
17:692:49607:16:17:72:540:152:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:update in the sender’s priors on whether the receiver is a xenophobe.  In our discussion of results,
17:693:49707:17:0:72:381:135:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:we provide suggestive evidence consistent with these hypotheses.
18:694:49773:0:24:72:181:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:3.3  Main Results
18:695:49790:24:16:72:540:666:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Appendix Table A.1 provides evidence that individual characteristics are balanced across all four
18:696:49887:16:17:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:pre-election experimental conditions, confirming that the randomization was successful.  The first
18:697:49985:17:16:72:540:633:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:four columns of Figure 1 display our main findings from the pre-election experiment.  In the control
18:698:50085:16:17:72:540:617:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:condition before the election, we observe a large and statistically significant wedge between dona-
18:699:50184:17:16:72:540:600:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:tion rates in private and in public:  a drop from 54% in private to 34% in public (the p-value of a
18:700:50283:16:16:72:540:584:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:t test of equality is 0.002).  Among individuals in the information condition, we observe no differ-
18:701:50383:16:17:72:540:568:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ence in private and public donation rates, which are 47% and 46%, respectively (p-value=0.839).
18:702:50478:17:16:72:540:551:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Moreover, we find no significant difference in private donation rates between the information and
18:703:50575:16:17:72:540:535:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:control conditions (p-value=0.280), suggesting that the information is not increasing privately-held
18:704:50675:17:16:72:540:518:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:xenophobia.  The increase in public donation rates between the two conditions is statistically sig-
18:705:50774:16:17:72:540:502:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:nificant (p-value=0.089), as is the difference in differences between donation rates in private across
18:706:50876:17:16:72:540:485:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:conditions and donation rates in public across conditions (p-value=0.050).  These results indicate
18:707:50974:16:16:72:540:469:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that the information provided causally increased the social acceptability of the action to the point
18:708:51074:16:17:72:540:453:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of eliminating the original social stigma associated with it.  The first two columns of Table 1 display
18:709:51177:17:16:72:540:436:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the difference in differences results in regression format and show that our results are unchanged
18:710:51275:16:17:72:540:420:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:when individual covariates are included.  The table also displays p-values from permutation tests,
18:711:51373:17:16:72:371:403:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:showing that our findings are robust to that inference method.
18:712:51435:16:17:88:539:387:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:As an additional way of examining the effect of Trump’s increased popularity on public expres-
18:713:51529:17:16:72:540:370:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:sion  of  the  xenophobic  action,  we  compare  the  private  and  public  donation  rates  in  the  control
18:714:51638:16:17:72:540:354:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:condition before and after the election.  In the last two columns of Figure 1, we analyze the actions
18:715:51739:17:16:72:540:337:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of respondents who participated in both waves of the experiment.  Though we focus on a subset of
18:716:51835:16:16:72:540:321:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the original participants, we find no evidence of selective attrition, and the samples in the different
18:717:51938:16:17:72:540:305:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:conditions  (before  and  after)  are  again  well  balanced  (see  Appendix  Table  A.2).   In  private,  we
18:718:52047:17:16:72:540:288:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:again observe no increase in donation rates (54% before the election and 49% after the election,
18:719:52143:16:17:72:540:272:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:p-value=0.440).  In public, we observe a significant increase from 34% before the election to 48%
18:720:52240:17:16:72:540:255:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:after it (p-value=0.060).  The difference in differences between donation rates in private before and
18:721:52341:16:17:72:540:239:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:after the election and donation rates in public before and after the election in the control condition
18:722:52443:17:16:72:540:222:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:is  also  statistically  significant  (p-value=0.062).   It  is  worth  emphasizing  that  the  donation  rates
18:723:52554:16:16:72:540:206:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:following  the  two  different  “treatments”  (either  experimental  or  natural)  are  extremely  similar:
18:724:52661:16:17:72:540:190:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:47% vs.  49% in private, and 46% vs.  48% in public.  The last two columns of Table 1 display the
18:725:52758:17:16:72:540:173:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:results in regression format, and again confirm that the findings are robust to using permutation
18:726:52855:16:17:72:540:157:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:tests.  Our results are also robust to different samples for the post-election experiment, such as also
18:727:52958:17:16:72:386:140:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f6:B:including new participants, as displayed in Appendix Table A.3.11
18:728:53023:16:14:80:539:124:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:11If we restrict the analysis to the 274 subjects who followed the registered protocol results are directionally similar:
18:729:53144:14:11:72:540:110:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:raw donation rates are respectively, for the the private and public groups, 54% and 35% in the control condition before
18:730:53263:11:0:72:540:99:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:the election, 50% and 39% in the information condition before the election, and 39% and 45% in the control condition
19:731:53381:0:24:72:164:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:3.4  Discussion
19:732:53396:24:23:72:231:666:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:C:3.4.1    Potential Mechanisms
19:733:53425:23:17:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:In the experimental intervention before the election, the information provided to participants gen-
19:734:53524:17:16:72:540:626:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:erated a positive (or null) update in their beliefs about Trump’s local popularity.  Although this
19:735:53622:16:17:72:540:610:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:might have also updated a participant’s belief regarding whether the surveyor is a xenophobe, we
19:736:53718:17:16:72:540:593:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:believe that the main effect of the information shock was to update a participant’s belief about
19:737:53814:16:16:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the surveyor’s priors about the share of xenophobes around the participant.  While we don’t have
19:738:53910:16:17:72:540:561:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a direct measure of this belief about the surveyor’s prior, we elicited the update in participants’
19:739:54009:17:16:72:540:544:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:beliefs about the share of xenophobes in their home state – a good proxy for the other variable.  For
19:740:54110:16:17:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the proxy to be valid, we need the update in participants’ beliefs about the share of xenophobes
19:741:54206:17:16:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in their state to go in thesame directionas the update in their beliefs about the surveyor’s beliefs
19:742:54306:16:17:72:383:495:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:about that same share.  We believe this a reasonable assumption.
19:743:54370:17:16:88:539:478:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Figure 2 provides evidence that the information shock led to a positive update in beliefs about
19:744:54465:16:17:72:540:462:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the opinions about other individuals in the same state.  In the control condition before the election,
19:745:54567:17:16:72:540:445:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the average guess was that 64% of other people in the participant’s home state would agree with the
19:746:54666:16:16:72:540:429:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:xenophobic statement, while it was 68% in the information condition (p-value=0.062).  This small
19:747:54762:16:17:72:540:413:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:increase in the average guess might not fully display the impact that the information intervention
19:748:54860:17:16:72:540:396:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:had on thedistributionof beliefs about others.  The distribution in the information condition first-
19:749:54960:16:17:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:order  stochastically  dominates  the  distribution  in  the  control  condition  (a  Kolmogorov-Smirnov
19:750:55064:17:16:72:540:363:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:test of equality of the two distributions yields a p-value of 0.072).  For example,  the percentage
19:751:55163:16:17:72:540:347:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of participants who think that the share of those agreeing with the xenophobic statement in their
19:752:55260:17:16:72:540:330:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:state is above 90% increases substantially with the provision of information (from 9% to 17%, with
19:753:55358:16:16:72:164:314:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a p-value of 0.018).
19:754:55378:16:17:88:539:298:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:When  we  analyze  the  effects  of  Trump’s  actual  victory  on  the  social  stigma  associated  with
19:755:55482:17:16:72:539:281:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the  donation  decision,  it  is  less  clearex  antethat  an  update  in  respondents’  beliefs  about  the
19:756:55590:16:17:71:539:265:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:surveyor’s  priors  regarding  the  share  of  xenophobes  in  the  respondents’  state  would  the  main
19:757:55695:17:16:71:539:248:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:driver of the findings.  After the election,  the surveyor is not directly providing any information
19:758:55795:16:17:71:539:232:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that would necessarily lead to an unambiguously weakly positive update in perceptions of Trump’s
19:759:55891:17:16:71:539:215:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:local  popularity.   For  example,  participants  might  now  believe  that  Trump’s  actual  margin  of
19:760:55995:16:16:71:539:199:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:victory in their state might was smaller than what the surveyor had originally expected.  Indeed,
19:761:56092:16:17:71:539:183:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:when comparing the pre-election control group with the group after the election, we find no shift in
19:762:56192:17:20:71:539:166:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the distribution of beliefs about the share of xenophobes in participants’ home states (see Appendix
19:763:56292:20:11:72:540:146:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:after the election.  As with the full sample, the wedge between the public and private condition is significant in the
19:764:56410:11:11:72:540:135:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:control condition before the election (p-value 0.018), and not significant in the information condition (p-value 0.219),
19:765:56530:11:11:72:540:124:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:or after the election (p-value 0.607).  The difference in differences between donation rates in private across conditions
19:766:56651:11:11:72:540:113:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:and donation rates in public across conditions is smaller than in the full sample and not significant before the election
19:767:56772:11:0:72:428:102:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:(8.4%, p-value 0.486), but large and significant after the election (24.9%, p-value 0.068).
20:768:56865:0:17:72:540:690:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Figure A.1). However, there is an unambiguously weakly positive update in participants’ perception
20:769:56963:17:16:72:540:673:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of  Trump’snationalpopularity.   According  to  our  model,  this  will  increase  the  probability  that
20:770:57068:16:17:72:540:657:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:participants:  (i) think that the surveyor is xenophobic, and (ii) think that the surveyor will judge
20:771:57169:17:16:72:540:640:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:them less negatively even if the researcher is not xenophobic.  Hence, although we do not provide
20:772:57266:16:16:72:540:624:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:direct evidence of these mechanisms, the nature of the intervention suggests that these two elements
20:773:57366:16:32:72:526:608:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:are the likely drivers of the findings in the comparison of pre- and post-election donation rates.
20:774:57464:32:24:72:296:576:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:C:3.4.2    Further Interpreting the Findings
20:775:57506:24:16:72:540:552:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Although  the  effects  we  find  are  extremely  large,  it  is  important  to  note  that  they  are  coming
20:776:57616:16:17:72:540:536:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:from  a  marginal  positive  signal  of  Trump’s  local  popularity  starting  from  a  situation  where  he
20:777:57724:17:16:72:540:519:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:was already believed to be extremely popular locally.  Even in the control condition, the average
20:778:57821:16:16:72:540:503:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:individual believes that 64% of people in his/her state agree with the xenophobic statement, and
20:779:57917:16:17:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:34% of participants make the donation in public.  Though we cannot test this hypothesis, perhaps
20:780:58013:17:16:72:540:470:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:an increase in the perceived popularity of holding xenophobic views and a reduction of the related
20:781:58111:16:17:72:540:454:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:social  stigma  might  have  already  taken  place  throughout  the  presidential  campaign,  before  the
20:782:58216:17:16:72:540:437:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:experiment took place.  It is also possible that the statement we chose might have been perceived as
20:783:58316:16:17:72:540:421:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:relatively mild toward the end of the campaign period, so the small update in beliefs about the views
20:784:58417:17:16:72:540:404:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of others regarding the chosen statement could correspond to larger updates for a more extreme
20:785:58511:16:16:72:540:388:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:statement.  Of course, we cannot estimate how large the effects of our experiment would have been
20:786:58608:16:17:72:540:372:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:had the baseline level of Trump’s perceived local popularity been lower (as in the beginning of the
20:787:58707:17:16:72:398:355:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:campaign season) and thus the effect of the signal possibly stronger.
20:788:58776:16:17:88:539:339:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Finally, we can rule out that our main effect is coming from participants updating their beliefs
20:789:58872:17:16:72:540:322:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:about the instrumental benefits associated with donating to the organization (for example, because
20:790:58970:16:17:72:540:306:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the organization is now more likely to fulfill its mission).  Any effect explained by that factor would
20:791:59073:17:38:72:309:289:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:have showed up in the private donation rates too.
20:792:59122:38:28:72:368:251:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:C:4  Auxiliary Experiment: Dictator Game
20:793:59160:28:23:72:226:223:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:4.1  Experimental Design
20:794:59184:23:24:72:422:200:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:C:4.1.1    Wave 1 – Non-Anonymous Behavior by the Swiss Player
20:795:59244:24:16:72:540:176:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:In late February 2017, we recruited participants from the six states in which Hillary Clinton won
20:796:59341:16:16:72:540:160:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the  presidential  election  with  the  highest  margin:  California,  Hawaii,  Maryland,  Massachusetts,
20:797:59446:16:17:72:540:144:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:New York, and Vermont.  This was done to maximize the chances of recruiting subjects with liberal
20:798:59543:17:16:72:389:127:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f6:B:views, and in particular subjects with no anti-Muslim sentiment.12
20:799:59609:16:15:80:539:111:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:12As in the main experiment, Turk workers with at least 80% approval rate could see our request, which in this case
20:800:59724:15:0:72:540:96:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:was described as a “4-5 minutes short survey” with a reward of $0.50.  Each worker could participate in the survey
21:801:59840:0:17:88:539:690:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:First, after answering a number of demographic questions, all participants were explained that a
21:802:59936:17:16:72:540:673:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:minaret is a tower typically built adjacent to a mosque and traditionally used for the Muslim call to
21:803:60037:16:17:72:540:657:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:prayer.  Second, they were asked whether they would support the introduction of a law prohibiting
21:804:60134:17:16:72:540:640:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the  building  of  minarets  in  their  state.   We  focus  on  subjects  who  reported  to  be  against  the
21:805:60243:16:16:72:540:624:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:introduction  of  this  law  (N  =  396),  and  we  examine  how  they  interact  with  a  person  who  has
21:806:60350:16:17:72:540:608:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:opposite views.  In order to do so, in the third part of the survey, participants were told they were
21:807:60451:17:16:72:540:591:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:matched  with  a  subject  from  another  survey  and  were  asked  to  play  a  dictator  game  in  which
21:808:60557:16:17:72:540:575:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:they  could  decide  how  to  split  $3  (half  of  an  hourly  wage  on  the  platform)  between  themselves
21:809:60666:17:16:72:540:558:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and the other participant.  We randomly assigned our participants to three different groups and
21:810:60761:16:17:72:540:542:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:randomized the background information we gave to our participants about the person they were
21:811:60853:17:16:72:540:525:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:matched  with.   Participants  in  the  control  group  were  only  told  that  the  participant  they  were
21:812:60961:16:17:72:540:509:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:matched with was a 24-year-old male from Switzerland.  Note that we used real 24-year-old male
21:813:61055:17:16:72:540:492:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:subjects from Switzerland recruited to take part of a short survey by a research assistant from the
21:814:61154:16:16:72:171:476:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:University of Zurich.
21:815:61175:16:17:88:539:460:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Participants  in  theanti-minaretsgroup  were  additionally  told  that  this  person  supports  the
21:816:61275:17:16:72:540:443:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f5:B:prohibition of the building of minarets in Switzerland.  Participants in theanti-minarets,  public
21:817:61373:16:17:72:540:427:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:supportgroup were instead told that “like 57.5% of Swiss respondents,  the participant supports
21:818:61468:17:31:72:355:410:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the prohibition of the building of minarets in Switzerland.”
21:819:61528:31:24:72:395:379:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:C:4.1.2    Wave 2 – Anonymous Behavior by the Swiss Player
21:820:61584:24:16:72:540:355:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f5:B:If we find higher donations in theAnti-minarets, public support group, when compared to theanti-
21:821:61680:16:17:72:540:339:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:minarets, we can conclude that the participants may believe that the Swiss person has strategic
21:822:61775:17:16:72:540:322:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:reasons to state that he is anti-minarets, and for this reason judge him less for expressing that view.
21:823:61878:16:17:72:540:306:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:However, a potential alternative interpretation for this result is that participants might judge the
21:824:61978:17:16:72:539:289:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f5:B:Swiss person less negatively when the majority of Swiss support the ban,regardless of whether his
21:825:62075:16:17:72:540:273:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:support  was  expressed  in  public.For example, it could be that participants feel that they cannot
21:826:62175:17:16:72:540:256:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:blame a person for privately holding a view if that person is surrounded by many other people who
21:827:62272:16:16:72:508:240:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:also hold that view and who could also have influenced the private opinions of that person.
21:828:62363:16:17:88:539:224:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:To explicitly rule out this possibility, we conducted a slightly modified version of our protocol on
21:829:62463:17:16:72:540:207:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the days immediately following the first wave of the dictator game experiment.  In the second wave,
21:830:62562:16:17:72:540:191:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:participants were informed about the fact that the 24-year-old male from Switzerland expressed his
21:831:62660:17:16:72:540:174:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:opinion in ananonymoussurvey.  As in the original version, we recruited participants from the six
21:832:62757:16:17:72:540:158:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:states in which Hillary Clinton won the presidential election with the highest margin (California,
21:833:62855:17:20:72:540:141:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Hawaii, Maryland, Massachusetts, New York, and Vermont).  To make sure we could recruit enough
21:834:62949:20:11:72:540:121:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:only once.  Workers who clicked on the request were displayed detailed instructions about the task, and given access
21:835:63065:11:11:72:540:110:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:to  links  to  the  study  information  sheet  and  the  actual  survey.   The  survey  was  conducted  on  the  online  platform
21:836:63194:11:0:72:471:99:9:g_d0_f18:9:g_d0_f8:F:Qualtrics.  The script used in this auxiliary experiment is displayed in the Supplemental Appendix.
22:837:63295:0:17:72:540:690:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:participants, we also included six other states with a high share of votes for Clinton (Connecticut,
22:838:63395:17:16:72:383:673:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f6:B:Delaware, Illinois, New Jersey, Rhode Island, and Washington).13
22:839:63459:16:17:88:539:657:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The  design  of  this  experiment  was  almost  identical  to  the  original  version.   Once  again,  we
22:840:63564:17:16:72:540:640:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:focus on subjects who reported to be against the introduction of the ban (N = 427).  The main
22:841:63657:16:16:72:540:624:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:difference  with  the  original  version,  is  that  we  emphasized  how  the  Swiss  participant  expressed
22:842:63765:16:17:72:540:608:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:his opinion anonymously.  Instead of writing as before that “we matched you with a participant
22:843:63859:17:16:72:540:591:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:from another survey”, in this version we wrote “we matched you with a participant from another
22:844:63953:16:17:72:540:575:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:anonymous survey.” In our treatment groups we emphasized once again that the survey the Swiss
22:845:64046:17:16:72:540:558:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:participants  participated  in  was  anonymous:   “In  our  anonymous  survey,  like  the  one  you  just
22:846:64151:16:17:72:540:542:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:completed, he said he supports the prohibition of the building of minarets in Switzerland.” We call
22:847:64250:17:16:72:539:525:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:this  first  treatment  group  theanonymous  anti-minaretsgroup.   Finally,  instead  of  writing  “like
22:848:64354:16:17:72:540:509:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:57.5% of Swiss respondents, the participant supports the prohibition of the building of minarets in
22:849:64453:17:16:72:540:492:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Switzerland” in this case we wrote “According to numbers from 2009, 57.5% of Swiss respondents
22:850:64547:16:16:72:540:476:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:are  in  favor  of  prohibiting  the  building  of  minarets.”  We  call  this  second  treatment  group  the
22:851:64656:16:32:72:309:460:11:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:C:anonymous anti-minarets, public supportgroup.14
22:852:64703:32:24:72:222:428:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:C:4.1.3    Elicitation of Beliefs
22:853:64734:24:16:72:540:404:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:At the end of the intervention,  subjects in the control group were also asked about their beliefs
22:854:64832:16:16:72:540:388:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:regarding the share of the Swiss population who supports banning the construction of minarets,
22:855:64926:16:17:72:540:372:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and  whether  they  believed  the  ban  is  legal  in  Switzerland.   In  the  first  wave  we  did  not  collect
22:856:65039:17:16:72:540:355:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:this information for individuals in theanti-minaretsandanti-minarets public supportgroups.  To
22:857:65133:16:17:72:540:339:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:check  whether  their  beliefs  about  the  share  of  the  Swiss  population  supporting  the  ban  are  not
22:858:65242:17:16:72:540:322:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:changed by the treatments, we included both the control group and the treatment groups in the
22:859:65335:16:17:72:540:306:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:second wave.  The share thinking that a majority of Swiss support the ban is almost identical in
22:860:65431:17:16:72:539:289:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the control group and theanti-minaretsgroup (respectively 20 and 25%,  with a p-value for the
22:861:65524:16:15:80:539:273:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:13As in the other two experiments, Turk workers with at least 80% approval rate could see our request, which in
22:862:65635:15:11:72:540:258:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:this case was described as a “4-5 minutes short survey” with a reward of $0.50.  Each worker could participate in the
22:863:65752:11:11:72:540:247:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:survey only once, and only if she did not participate in our other experiment.  Workers who clicked on the request
22:864:65866:11:11:72:540:236:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:were displayed detailed instructions about the task, and given access to links to the study information sheet and the
22:865:65983:11:11:72:539:225:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:actual survey.  The survey was conducted on the online platformQualtrics.  The script used in this second wave of
22:866:66096:11:7:72:350:214:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:the auxiliary experiment is displayed in the Supplemental Appendix.
22:867:66163:7:15:80:539:207:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:14Our design also included a fourth group (N=136 in wave 1, and N=139 in wave 2), where participants were instead
22:868:66276:15:11:72:540:192:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:told:  “Building minarets is illegal in Switzerland,  following a 2009 referendum.  Like 57.5% of Swiss respondents,
22:869:66392:11:11:72:540:181:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:the  participant  supports  the  prohibition  of  the  building  of  minarets  in  Switzerland.   However,  he  did  not  vote  in
22:870:66522:11:11:72:540:170:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:the  referendum  since  he  was  under  legal  voting  age”  in  wave  1,  and  “In  our  anonymous  survey,  like  the  one  you
22:871:66651:11:11:72:540:159:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:just completed, he said he supports the prohibition of the building of minarets in Switzerland.  Building minarets is
22:872:66768:11:11:72:540:148:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:illegal in Switzerland, following a 2009 referendum.  According to numbers from 2009, 57.5% of Swiss respondents
22:873:66880:11:10:72:540:137:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:are in favor of prohibiting the building of minarets.  However, the person you are matched with did not vote in the
22:874:66995:10:11:72:540:127:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:referendum since he was under legal voting age” in wave 2.  This treatment was intended to test whether providing
22:875:67108:11:11:72:540:116:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:information that a view is not only held by a majority but is alsoofficialwould additionally change the donation
22:876:67220:11:11:72:540:105:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:rates.  We found no effect of this additional treatment relative to the second treatment group.  We report these results
22:877:67340:11:0:72:209:94:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:in Appendix Figures A.2 and A.3.
23:878:67374:0:17:72:540:690:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:test of equality of 0.301), but increases to 63% in theanti-minarets public supportgroup (p-values
23:879:67472:17:16:72:540:673:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of the test of equality are 0.000 against both groups).  The median belief about the share of the
23:880:67569:16:17:72:540:657:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Swiss population supporting the ban is 30% in both control andanti-minaretsgroups, and 55% in
23:881:67662:17:16:72:539:640:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:theanti-minarets public supportgroup.  This confirms that our experimental manipulation indeed
23:882:67756:16:16:72:445:624:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f6:B:shifted beliefs about the level of popular support for the ban in Switzerland.15
23:883:67836:16:17:88:540:608:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Participants across conditions were also asked whether they believed the construction of minarets
23:884:67933:17:16:72:540:591:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:is legal in Switzerland:  across the three groups, the majority reported to think that constructing
23:885:68032:16:17:72:540:575:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:minarets  was  legal  (88%  in  the  control  group,  77%  in  theanti-minaretsgroup,  and  74%  in  the
23:886:68136:17:16:72:540:558:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:anti-minarets  public  supportgroup).16We can thus rule out that the effects are affected by the
23:887:68232:16:17:72:540:542:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:fact that the ban is actually legal, and can thus isolate the role of public opinion on participants’
23:888:68333:17:32:72:213:525:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:judgment of the Swiss player.
23:889:68362:32:23:72:424:493:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:4.2  Linking the Experiment to the Theoretical Framework
23:890:68418:23:29:72:397:470:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We have the following predictions, which help us test Proposition 3.
23:891:68486:29:16:88:539:441:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f4:A:•Anti-minaretsgroup:  The  Swiss  person  is  revealed  to  be  anti-minarets.   The  participants’
23:892:68585:16:17:99:540:425:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:prior that Swiss people are on average anti-minarets is relatively low. This has two implica-
23:893:68678:17:16:99:540:408:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:tions.  First, before the information about the Swiss person is communicated, the perceived
23:894:68769:16:16:99:540:392:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:probability that he is anti-minarets is low.  Second, and more importantly, he is not thought
23:895:68862:16:17:99:540:376:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:to have strategic reasons to pretend to be anti-minarets, because this view is not thought to
23:896:68955:17:16:99:540:359:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:be popular among citizens in Switzerland (the subjects believe that the equilibrium that this
23:897:69048:16:17:99:539:343:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Swiss person faces would imply that he will only saymi=Aif he indeed has typeti=A).
23:898:69131:17:16:99:540:326:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Thus, the posterior that this person is anti-minarets increases all the way to 1.  This lowers
23:899:69225:16:26:99:326:310:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:donations when compared to the control group.
23:900:69270:26:16:88:539:284:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f4:A:•Anti-minarets,  public  supportgroup:  The Swiss person is revealed to be anti-minarets, and
23:901:69363:16:16:99:540:268:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:also we also reveal that 57% of Swiss respondents support banning minarets.  Now, compared
23:902:69453:16:17:99:540:252:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:to the previous experimental condition, the participants may believe that the Swiss person
23:903:69543:17:16:99:539:235:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:has strategic reasons to state that he is anti-minarets. This decreases Prj(ti=A|mi=A)
23:904:69629:16:17:99:539:219:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:from 1 to some value which, however, must be greater than12, as follows from Proposition 3.
23:905:69720:17:16:99:540:202:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:This implies that donations should be higher than in the previous treatment group, but not
23:906:69810:16:16:99:249:186:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:as high as in the control group.
23:907:69842:16:15:80:539:170:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:15Here we report the numbers from the second wave of the experiment, since the first wave only asked beliefs in
23:908:69953:15:11:72:540:155:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:the control group.  The numbers for this group are very similar across waves; for example, in the first wave, 17% of
23:909:70069:11:11:72:540:144:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:control group participants believe a majority of Swiss people support the ban, compared to 20% in the second wave.
23:910:70183:11:7:72:326:133:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:The median belief is 30% for the control groups in both waves.
23:911:70245:7:15:80:539:126:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:16While the beliefs are significantly different when comparing the control group with either of the two treatment
23:912:70358:15:11:72:540:111:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:groups (the p-values for the test of equality are 0.013 against theanonymous anti-minaretsgroup and 0.002 against
23:913:70471:11:11:72:540:100:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:theanonymous anti-minarets public support group), there is no statistical difference between the two treatment groups
23:914:70588:11:0:72:253:89:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:(the p-value for the test of equality is 0.500).
24:915:70638:0:17:99:540:690:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The second wave of the experiment helps us further test our model and rule out the main
24:916:70725:17:25:99:222:673:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:alternative interpretation:
24:917:70752:25:17:88:539:648:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f4:A:•Anonymous anti-minaretsgroup:  The Swiss person is revealed to beprivatelyanti-minarets.
24:918:70841:17:16:99:540:631:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Again, subjects’ prior that Swiss people are on average anti-minarets is relatively low.  The
24:919:70934:16:16:99:540:615:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:posterior that the Swiss player is anti-minarets is 1,  so donations should be similar to the
24:920:71027:16:26:99:254:599:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:ones in theAnti-minarets group.
24:921:71058:26:16:88:539:573:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f5:A:•Anonymous  anti-minarets,  public  supportgroup:   The  Swiss  person  is  revealed  to  bepri-
24:922:71154:16:17:99:540:557:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:A:vatelyanti-minarets, and also we also reveal that 57% of Swiss respondents support banning
24:923:71244:17:16:99:540:540:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:minarets.  Unlike the non-anonymous version of this treatment, participants do not think the
24:924:71336:16:17:99:540:524:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Swiss person has strategic reasons to state that he is anti-minarets, since the expression is
24:925:71429:17:16:99:540:507:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:anonymous.  As a result, the posterior that the Swiss player is against anti-minarets is again
24:926:71523:16:32:99:480:491:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:1 and the donation levels should be similar to those in theAnti-minarets group.
24:927:71602:32:24:72:146:459:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:4.3  Results
24:928:71614:24:16:72:540:435:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Appendix Table A.4 provides a test of balance of individual characteristics across all six conditions
24:929:71715:16:17:72:540:419:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:from the two waves and separately for the three conditions of each wave.  Although the two waves
24:930:71811:17:16:72:540:402:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:were  not  conducted  simultaneously,  the  variables  are  fairly  well-balanced  when  pooling  the  two
24:931:71917:16:16:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:waves.   Only  the  share  of  white  respondents  is  marginally  unbalanced  (p-value  of  0.085).   As
24:932:72022:16:17:72:540:370:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a result, to simplify the exposition of our findings, below we pool the observations in the control
24:933:72121:17:16:72:540:353:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:groups from the two waves, and compare the raw outcome variables across the two waves. Appendix
24:934:72216:16:17:72:540:337:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Figures A.4 and A.5 display the results separately for the two waves of the experiment and show
24:935:72311:17:16:72:383:320:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that the numbers are almost identical for the two control groups.
24:936:72376:16:17:88:539:304:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:We now turn to the main findings from the auxiliary experiment, displayed in Figure 3.  Panel
24:937:72469:17:16:72:540:287:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:A displays comparisons of average donations across groups.  In the control condition, where partic-
24:938:72568:16:16:72:540:271:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ipants are only told that they are matched with a 24-year-old male from Switzerland, we observe
24:939:72663:16:17:72:540:255:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:an average transfer to the Swiss participant of $1.03.  The average transfer is substantially lower
24:940:72762:17:16:72:539:238:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:for subjects in theanti-minaretsgroup, who are also told that this person supports the prohibition
24:941:72860:16:17:72:540:222:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:on  building  minarets  in  Switzerland:  the  average  transfer  for  this  group  is  $0.69.   The  effect  of
24:942:72972:17:16:72:540:205:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:informing subject about the anti-Muslim views of the Swiss participant is statistically significant
24:943:73071:16:17:72:540:189:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f5:B:(p-value=0.000).  However, the average transfer among subjects in theanti-minarets, public support
24:944:73169:17:16:72:540:172:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:group who are told that the majority of Swiss respondents are against minarets is $0.92,  which
24:945:73264:16:17:72:540:156:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:is not statistically different from the average transfer in the control group (the p-value of the dif-
24:946:73366:17:16:72:539:139:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ference is 0.162) but is substantially higher than the average transfer in theanti-minaretsgroup
24:947:73462:16:16:72:539:123:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(p-value=0.013).  The average donation in theanonymous anti-minaretsgroup is identical to that
24:948:73556:16:17:72:539:107:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f5:B:in theanti-minaretsgroup, at $0.69.  The average donation in theanonymous anti-minarets, public
24:949:73651:17:0:72:539:90:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:supportgroup is also very similar:  $0.70.  These two levels are significantly different from the av-
25:950:73754:0:17:72:540:690:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f5:B:erage in the control group (p-value=0.000 in both cases).  The average donation in theanonymous
25:951:73849:17:16:72:539:673:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:anti-minarets, public supportgroup is also significantly lower than the one in the first-wave version
25:952:73950:16:17:72:233:657:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of the treatment (p-value=0.014).
25:953:73983:17:16:88:540:640:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Panel B compares across conditions the share of participants who donotshare any of their $3
25:954:74074:16:16:71:539:624:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:endowment with the Swiss person.  The percentage of participants deciding not to transfer anything
25:955:74172:16:17:71:539:608:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to the Swiss respondent increases from 22% in the control group to 42% in theanti-minaretsgroup
25:956:74267:17:16:71:540:591:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(p-value 0.000), while only 27% of subjects in theanti-minarets, public supportdecide to keep all $3.
25:957:74368:16:17:71:539:575:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:This percentage is not statistically different from the one in the control group (p-value=0.370), but
25:958:74469:17:16:71:539:558:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:is substantially lower than the one for subjects in theanti-minaretsgroup (p-value=0.013).  Here
25:959:74565:16:17:72:540:542:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:again,  the  levels  of  the  outcome  variable  in  the  two  anonymous  treatments  are  almost  identical
25:960:74673:17:16:72:539:525:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to  the  level  in  theanti-minaretsgroup:  43%  and  44%.   Importantly,  the  share  of  participants
25:961:74776:16:17:72:540:509:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:not  donating  is  significantly  higher  in  theanonymous  anti-minarets,  public  supportgroup  when
25:962:74878:17:16:72:430:492:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:compared to the non-anonymous version of the treatment (p-value=0.004).
25:963:74949:16:16:88:539:476:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Panel C displays a similar pattern for the median transfer, which is $1.50 in the control group,
25:964:75045:16:17:72:539:460:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:$0.30 in theanti-minaretsgroup, and $1.20 in theanti-minarets, public supportgroup.  While the
25:965:75139:17:16:72:540:443:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:median transfer in the control group is higher than the median transfer in both other groups (p-value
25:966:75240:16:17:72:540:427:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:against theanti-minaretsis 0.000 and against theanti-minarets  public,  supportgroup is 0.030),
25:967:75335:17:16:72:540:410:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:providing information about the fact that 57.5% of Swiss respondents support the prohibition on
25:968:75430:16:17:72:540:394:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:building minarets makes a statistically significant difference (p-value 0.000), when compared to the
25:969:75530:17:16:72:540:377:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:anti-minaretsgroup.   The  median  donation  in  the  two  anonymous  groups  are  identical  ($0.50).
25:970:75632:16:16:72:539:361:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The median donation in theanonymous anti-minaretsgroup is not significantly different from the
25:971:75726:16:17:72:539:345:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f5:B:median in theanti-minaretsgroup (p-value 0.496).  The median donation in theanonymous anti-
25:972:75817:17:16:72:540:328:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:F:minarets,  public  supportgroup is significantly lower than the median in theanti-minarets,  public
25:973:75916:16:17:72:193:312:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:supportgroup (p=0.021).
25:974:75939:17:16:88:539:295:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Overall, across all three outcome variables, the results confirm the four predictions stemming
25:975:76033:16:17:72:540:279:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:from the model.  Appendix Table A.5 displays the results in regression format and show that our
25:976:76128:17:38:72:370:262:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:results are unchanged when individual covariates are included.
25:977:76190:38:27:72:173:224:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:C:5  Conclusion
25:978:76203:27:16:72:540:197:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We show that a positive update in people’s beliefs about Donald Trump’s popularity increases their
25:979:76301:16:17:72:540:181:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:willingness to publicly express xenophobic views.  Building on a simple model of communication
25:980:76395:17:16:72:540:164:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and on a second auxiliary experiment with a dictator game, we also provide suggestive evidence of
25:981:76492:16:17:72:540:148:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the mechanisms behind the effects.  By aggregating information about individuals’ private views,
25:982:76588:17:16:72:540:131:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:elections  can  update  positively  people’s  perceptions  about  the  share  of  people  who  support  an
25:983:76694:16:17:72:540:115:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:opinion previously believed to be stigmatized.  This may in turn change people’s perceptions about
25:984:76792:17:0:72:388:98:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the negative judgement they will face for expressing their opinion.
26:985:76861:0:17:88:539:690:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Though beyond the scope of our study,  the potential interaction between private and public
26:986:76952:17:16:72:540:673:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:opinions might exacerbate the effects of events that trigger changes in the social acceptability of
26:987:77051:16:17:72:540:657:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:holding particular views.  Moreover, higher electoral support for a candidate associated with certain
26:988:77152:17:16:72:540:640:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:views might shape individuals’ perceptions of the social desirability of those views,  regardless of
26:989:77252:16:16:72:298:624:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:whether or not the candidate wins the election.
26:990:77299:16:17:88:539:608:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Our  findings  shed  light  on  the  factors  that  can  trigger  rapid  change  in  social  norms,  and  in
26:991:77407:17:16:72:540:591:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:particular,  norms  against  the  expression  of  xenophobic  views.   Our  results  suggest  that  social
26:992:77513:16:17:72:540:575:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:norms regarding the expression of such views in the U.S. might have already been causally changed
26:993:77610:17:16:72:540:558:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:by Trump’s rise in popularity and eventual electoral victory.  More broadly,  the mechanisms we
26:994:77705:16:17:72:540:542:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:study  in  this  paper  might  help  explain  the  rise  –  and  potential  consequences  –  of  other  crucial
26:995:77816:17:16:72:540:525:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:recent events such as the Brexit vote in the UK, and more generally the rise in anti-immigrant and
26:996:77914:16:0:72:300:509:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:anti-minority sentiment in the developed world.
